Q: Which is more plausible, X or Y, as the sentence that will come between R and S?
R: Jane was a professor teaching piano to students.
S: Jane spent the morning sipping coffee and reading a book.
X: Two of Jane's students were early for their lessons.
Y: None of Jane's students had a lesson that day.
A: Let's think step by step.

First, we know that Jane was a professor teaching piano to students. This means that she had students who were taking lessons from her. 

Next, we see that in sentence S, Jane spent the morning sipping coffee and reading a book. This tells us that she had some free time in the morning. 

Now, let's consider the two options for the sentence that will come between R and S: 

X: Two of Jane's students were early for their lessons. 

This option seems plausible because it fits with the fact that Jane was a professor teaching piano to students. It's possible that some of her students were early for their lessons, and this could have happened before Jane spent the morning sipping coffee and reading a book. 

Y: None of Jane's students had a lesson that day. 

This option seems less plausible because it contradicts the fact that Jane was a professor teaching piano to students. If none of her students had a lesson that day, then it's unclear why Jane would be spending her morning sipping coffee and reading a book. 

Therefore, option X is more plausible as the sentence that will come between R and S. 
Therefore, the answer isX: Two of Jane's students were early for their lessons.
